<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Detailed_list">Detailed list</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Detailed list">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>To help compare different orders of magnitude, the following list describes various lengths between 1.6<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>−35</sup> meters and <span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mn>10</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msup>
<mn>10</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msup>
<mn>10</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>122</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle 10^{10^{10^{122}}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="10^{10^{10^{122}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f0da4c6feb5287d705dc0f51c21317c5ddbce34b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.901ex; height:3.509ex;"/></span>meters.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subatomic">Subatomic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Subatomic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span id="lt_1E-15"></span></p>
<table border="1" cellpadding="3px" class="wikitable">
<tr>
<th>Factor (<a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a>)</th>
<th>Multiple</th>
<th>Value</th>
<th>Item</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>10<sup>−35</sup></td>
<td>1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planck_Length" title="Planck Length">Planck Length</a></td>
<td>0.0000000000162 ym (1.62<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>−35</sup> m)</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Planck_length" title="Planck length">Planck length</a>; typical scale of hypothetical <a href="/wiki/Loop_quantum_gravity" title="Loop quantum gravity">loop quantum gravity</a> or size of a hypothetical <a href="/wiki/String_(physics)" title="String (physics)">string</a> and of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Branes" title="Branes">branes</a>; according to <a href="/wiki/String_theory" title="String theory">string theory</a> lengths smaller than this do not make any <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physical</a> sense.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burgess_and_Quevedo_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burgess_and_Quevedo-2">[2]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Quantum_foam" title="Quantum foam">Quantum foam</a> is thought to exist at this level.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>10<sup>−24</sup></td>
<td>1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yoctometer" title="Yoctometer">yoctometer</a> (ym)</td>
<td>20 ym (2 × 10<sup>−23</sup> meters)</td>
<td>Effective <a href="/wiki/Cross_section_(physics)" title="Cross section (physics)">cross section</a> radius of 1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MeV" title="MeV">MeV</a> <a href="/wiki/Neutrino" title="Neutrino">neutrinos</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="3">10<sup>−21</sup></td>
<td rowspan="3">1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zeptometer" title="Zeptometer">zeptometer</a> (zm)</td>
<td></td>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preons" title="Preons">Preons</a>, hypothetical particles proposed as subcomponents of quarks and leptons; the upper bound for the width of a <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_string" title="Cosmic string">cosmic string</a> in string theory.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>7 zm (7 × 10<sup>−21</sup> meters)</td>
<td>Effective cross section radius of high energy <a href="/wiki/Neutrino" title="Neutrino">neutrinos</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NaveN3_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-NaveN3-4">[4]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>310 zm (3.10 × 10<sup>−19</sup> meters)</td>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/De_Broglie_wavelength" title="De Broglie wavelength">De Broglie wavelength</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protons" title="Protons">protons</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">Large Hadron Collider</a> (4 TeV as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="3">10<sup>−18</sup></td>
<td rowspan="3">1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Attometer" title="Attometer">attometer</a> (am)</td>
<td rowspan="3"></td>
<td>Upper limit for the size of <a href="/wiki/Quark" title="Quark">quarks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electron" title="Electron">electrons</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Sensitivity of the <a href="/wiki/LIGO" title="LIGO">LIGO</a> detector for <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_wave" title="Gravitational wave">gravitational waves</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Upper bound of the typical size range for "fundamental <a href="/wiki/String_(physics)" title="String (physics)">strings</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burgess_and_Quevedo_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Burgess_and_Quevedo-2">[2]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="1">10<sup>−17</sup></td>
<td rowspan="1">10 am</td>
<td rowspan="1"></td>
<td>Range of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weak_force" title="Weak force">weak force</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="1">10<sup>−16</sup></td>
<td rowspan="1">100 am</td>
<td rowspan="1">850 am</td>
<td>approximate proton radius<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_to_astronomical_scale">Human to astronomical scale</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Human to astronomical scale">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table border="1" cellpadding="3px" class="wikitable">

<td rowspan="3">1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meter" title="Meter">meter</a></td>
<td>1 m (exactly)</td>
<td>Since 1983<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, defined as length of the path travelled by light in <a href="/wiki/Vacuum" title="Vacuum">vacuum</a> during a time interval of 1/299 792 458 of a <a href="/wiki/Second" title="Second">second</a>. See <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_metre" title="History of the metre">History of the metre</a> for previous definitions.</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1_megametre">1 megametre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1 megametre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1e6m_comparison_Mars_Mercury_Moon_Pluto_Haumea_-_no_transparency.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1280" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/1e6m_comparison_Mars_Mercury_Moon_Pluto_Haumea_-_no_transparency.png/220px-1e6m_comparison_Mars_Mercury_Moon_Pluto_Haumea_-_no_transparency.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/1e6m_comparison_Mars_Mercury_Moon_Pluto_Haumea_-_no_transparency.png/330px-1e6m_comparison_Mars_Mercury_Moon_Pluto_Haumea_-_no_transparency.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/1e6m_comparison_Mars_Mercury_Moon_Pluto_Haumea_-_no_transparency.png/440px-1e6m_comparison_Mars_Mercury_Moon_Pluto_Haumea_-_no_transparency.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1e6m_comparison_Mars_Mercury_Moon_Pluto_Haumea_-_no_transparency.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Small planets, the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet" title="Dwarf planet">dwarf planets</a> in our solar system have diameters from one to ten million metres. Top row: <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> (left), <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">Mercury</a> (right); bottom row: <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a> (left), <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a> (center), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haumea_(dwarf_planet)" title="Haumea (dwarf planet)">Haumea</a> (right), to scale.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To help compare different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude" title="Orders of magnitude">orders of magnitude</a> this page lists <a href="/wiki/Length" title="Length">lengths</a> starting at 10<sup>6</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> (1 <a href="/wiki/Megametre" title="Megametre">Mm</a> or 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Kilometre" title="Kilometre">km</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conversions">Conversions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Conversions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1 megametre is equal to:</p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_E%2B6_m" title="1 E+6 m">1 E+6 m</a> (one million metres)</li>
<li>approximately 621.37 <a href="/wiki/Mile" title="Mile">miles</a></li>
<li>Side of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Square_(geometry)" title="Square (geometry)">square</a> with area <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_E%2B12_m%C2%B2" title="1 E+12 m²">1,000,000 km<sup>2</sup></a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human-defined_scales_and_structures">Human-defined scales and structures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Human-defined scales and structures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>2.100 Mm — Length of proposed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iran-Pakistan-India_gas_pipeline" title="Iran-Pakistan-India gas pipeline">gas pipeline from Iran to India via Pakistan</a></li>
<li>2.288 Mm — Length of the official <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Highway" title="Alaska Highway">Alaska Highway</a> when it was built in the 1940s<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>3.069 Mm — Length of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95" title="Interstate 95">Interstate 95</a> (from <a href="/wiki/Houlton,_Maine" title="Houlton, Maine">Houlton, Maine</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami,_Florida" title="Miami, Florida">Miami, Florida</a>)</li>
<li>3.846 Mm — Length of <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1" title="U.S. Route 1">U.S. Route 1</a> (from <a href="/wiki/Fort_Kent,_Maine" title="Fort Kent, Maine">Fort Kent, Maine</a> to <a href="/wiki/Key_West,_Florida" title="Key West, Florida">Key West, Florida</a>)</li>
<li>5.007 Mm — Estimated length of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_90" title="Interstate 90">Interstate 90</a> (Seattle, Washington to Boston, Massachusetts)</li>
<li>5.614 Mm — Length of the Australian <a href="/wiki/Dingo_Fence" title="Dingo Fence">Dingo Fence</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li>7.821 Mm — Length of the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Canada_Highway" title="Trans-Canada Highway">Trans-Canada Highway</a>, the world's longest national highway (from <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria, British Columbia</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._John%27s,_Newfoundland" title="St. John's, Newfoundland">St. John's, Newfoundland</a>)</li>
<li>8.836 Mm — Road distance between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prudhoe_Bay" title="Prudhoe Bay">Prudhoe Bay</a>, Alaska, and <a href="/wiki/Key_West,_Florida" title="Key West, Florida">Key West, Florida</a>, the endpoints of the U.S. road network</li>
<li>8.852 Mm — Aggregate length of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">Great Wall of China</a>, including trenches, hills and rivers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup></li>
<li>9.259 Mm — Length of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_railway" title="Trans-Siberian railway">Trans-Siberian railway</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Munda_Biddi_Trail" title="Munda Biddi Trail">Munda Biddi Trail</a> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">WA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> is over 1000 km long - the world's longest off-road cycle trail</li>
<li>1.200 Mm — the length of the <a href="/wiki/Paris%E2%80%93Brest%E2%80%93Paris" title="Paris–Brest–Paris">Paris–Brest–Paris</a> bicycling event</li>
<li>Several endurance auto races are, or were, run for 1,000 km:
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bathurst_1000" title="Bathurst 1000">Bathurst 1000</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1000_km_Brands_Hatch" title="1000 km Brands Hatch">1000 km Brands Hatch</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1000_km_Buenos_Aires" title="1000 km Buenos Aires">1000 km Buenos Aires</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1000_km_Donington" title="1000 km Donington">1000 km Donington</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1000_km_Monza" title="1000 km Monza">1000 km Monza</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1000_km_N%C3%BCrburgring" title="1000 km Nürburgring">1000 km Nürburgring</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1000_km_Silverstone" title="1000 km Silverstone">1000 km Silverstone</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1000_km_Spa" title="1000 km Spa">1000 km Spa</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1000_km_Suzuka" title="1000 km Suzuka">1000 km Suzuka</a></li>

</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical">Geographical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geographical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>1.010 Mm — Distance from <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Paso" title="El Paso">El Paso</a> <a href="/wiki/As_the_crow_flies" title="As the crow flies">as the crow flies</a></li>
<li>2.000 Mm — Distance from <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> <a href="/wiki/As_the_crow_flies" title="As the crow flies">as the crow flies</a></li>
<li>2.800 Mm — Narrowest width of <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> (Brazil-West Africa)</li>
<li>2.850 Mm — Length of the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> river</li>
<li>2.205 Mm — Length of <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Sweden" title="Geography of Sweden">Sweden</a>'s total land boundaries</li>
<li>2.515 Mm — Length of <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Norway" title="Geography of Norway">Norway</a>'s total land boundaries</li>
<li>3.690 Mm — Length of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volga" title="Volga">Volga</a> river, longest in Europe</li>
<li>4.350 Mm — Length of the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a></li>
<li>4.715 Mm — Length of the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a></li>
<li>4.800 Mm — Widest width of <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> (U.S.-Northern Africa)</li>
<li>5.100 Mm — Distance from <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> to New York as the crow flies</li>
<li>6.270 Mm — Length of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi</a>-<a href="/wiki/Missouri_River" title="Missouri River">Missouri River</a> system</li>
<li>6.380 Mm — Length of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a></li>
<li>6.762 Mm — Length of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon</a> system, longest on <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a></li>
<li>8.200 Mm — Distance from <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> to San Francisco as the crow flies</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Astronomical_2">Astronomical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Astronomical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>1.000 Mm — Estimated shortest axis of <a href="/wiki/Ellipsoid" title="Ellipsoid">triaxial</a> <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet" title="Dwarf planet">dwarf planet</a> <a href="/wiki/Haumea" title="Haumea">Haumea</a></li>
<li>1.186 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Charon_(moon)" title="Charon (moon)">Charon</a>, the largest moon of <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a></li>
<li>1.280 Mm — Diameter of the trans-Neptunian object <a href="/wiki/50000_Quaoar" title="50000 Quaoar">50000 Quaoar</a></li>
<li>1.436 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Iapetus_(moon)" title="Iapetus (moon)">Iapetus</a>, one of <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a>'s major moons</li>
<li>1.578 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Titania_(moon)" title="Titania (moon)">Titania</a>, the largest of <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a>' moons</li>
<li>1.960 Mm — Estimated longest axis of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haumea_(dwarf_planet)" title="Haumea (dwarf planet)">Haumea</a></li>
<li>2.320 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a></li>
<li>2.400 Mm — Diameter of the dwarf planet <a href="/wiki/Eris_(dwarf_planet)" title="Eris (dwarf planet)">Eris</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/Trans-Neptunian_object" title="Trans-Neptunian object">trans-Neptunian object</a> found to date</li>
<li>2.707 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Triton_(moon)" title="Triton (moon)">Triton</a>, largest moon of <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a></li>
<li>3.122 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Europa_(moon)" title="Europa (moon)">Europa</a>, the smallest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galilean_satellite" title="Galilean satellite">Galilean satellite</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a></li>
<li>3.475 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a></li>
<li>3.643 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Io_(moon)" title="Io (moon)">Io</a>, a moon of Jupiter</li>
<li>4.821 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Callisto_(moon)" title="Callisto (moon)">Callisto</a>, a moon of Jupiter</li>
<li>4.879 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">Mercury</a></li>
<li>5.150 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">Titan</a>, the largest moon of Saturn</li>
<li>5.262 Mm — Diameter of Jupiter's moon <a href="/wiki/Ganymede_(moon)" title="Ganymede (moon)">Ganymede</a>, the largest moon in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_system" title="Solar system">solar system</a></li>
<li>6.366 Mm — <a href="/wiki/Earth_radius" title="Earth radius">Radius of Earth</a></li>
<li>6.792 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="10_megametres">10 megametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 10 megametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1e7m_comparison_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1280" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/1e7m_comparison_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus.png/220px-1e7m_comparison_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/1e7m_comparison_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus.png/330px-1e7m_comparison_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/1e7m_comparison_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus.png/440px-1e7m_comparison_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1e7m_comparison_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Planets from Venus up to Uranus have diameters from ten to one hundred million metres. Top row: <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a> (left), <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a> (right); middle row: <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a> (left), <a href="/wiki/Sirius#Sirius_B" title="Sirius">Sirius B</a> (center), and <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a> (right), to scale.</div>

<p>To help compare different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude" title="Orders of magnitude">orders of magnitude</a>, this page lists <a href="/wiki/Length" title="Length">lengths</a> starting at 10<sup>7</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">metres</a> (10 <a href="/wiki/Megametre" title="Megametre">megametres</a> or 10,000 <a href="/wiki/Kilometre" title="Kilometre">kilometres</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conversions_2">Conversions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Conversions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>10 megametres (10 Mm) is</p>
<ul>
<li>6,215 <a href="/wiki/Mile" title="Mile">miles</a>.</li>
<li>side of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Square_(geometry)" title="Square (geometry)">square</a> of area <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_E%2B14_m%C2%B2" title="1 E+14 m²">100,000,000</a> <a href="/wiki/Square_kilometre" title="Square kilometre">square kilometres</a> (km<sup>2</sup>)</li>
<li>radius of a <a href="/wiki/Circle" title="Circle">circle</a> of area 314,159,265 km<sup>2</sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human-defined_scales_and_structures_2">Human-defined scales and structures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Human-defined scales and structures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>11.085 Mm — Length of the <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>-<a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">Vladivostok</a> railway, a longer variant of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_railway" title="Trans-Siberian railway">Trans-Siberian railway</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup></li>
<li>13.300 Mm — Length of roads being rehabilitated and widened under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Highway_Development_Project" title="National Highway Development Project">National Highway Development Project</a> (launched in 1998) in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a></li>
<li>39.000 Mm — Length of the <a href="/wiki/SEA-ME-WE_3" title="SEA-ME-WE 3">SEA-ME-WE 3</a> optical submarine telecommunications cable, joining 39 points between <a href="/wiki/Norden,_Lower_Saxony" title="Norden, Lower Saxony">Norden</a>, Germany and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Okinawa" title="Okinawa">Okinawa</a>, Japan</li>
<li>67.000 Mm — Total length of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Highways_(India)" title="National Highways (India)">National Highways in India</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_2">Geographical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Geographical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>10 Mm — Approximate altitude of the outer boundary of the <a href="/wiki/Exosphere" title="Exosphere">exosphere</a></li>
<li>10.001 Mm — Length of the <a href="/wiki/Meridian_arc" title="Meridian arc">meridian arc</a> from the <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">Equator</a> (the original definition of the <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">metre</a> was based on this length).</li>
<li>60.000 Mm — Total length of the <a href="/wiki/Mid-ocean_ridge" title="Mid-ocean ridge">mid-ocean ridges</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Astronomical_3">Astronomical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Astronomical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>12.000 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Sirius" title="Sirius">Sirius B</a>, a <a href="/wiki/White_dwarf" title="White dwarf">white dwarf</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup></li>
<li>12.104 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a></li>
<li>12.742 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a></li>
<li>12.900 Mm — Minimum distance of the <a href="/wiki/Meteoroid" title="Meteoroid">meteoroid</a> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2004_FU162" title="2004 FU162">2004 FU<span style="position: relative; top: 0.3em;"><span style="font-size:80%;">162</span></span></a></span> from the center of Earth on March 31, 2004, closest on record</li>
<li>14.000 Mm — Smallest diameter of Jupiter's <a href="/wiki/Great_Red_Spot" title="Great Red Spot">Great Red Spot</a></li>
<li>34.770 Mm — Minimum distance of the <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">asteroid</a> <a href="/wiki/99942_Apophis" title="99942 Apophis">99942 Apophis</a> on April 13, 2029 from the center of Earth</li>
<li>35.786 Mm — Altitude of <a href="/wiki/Geostationary_orbit" title="Geostationary orbit">geostationary orbit</a></li>
<li>40.005 Mm — Polar circumference of the <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a></li>
<li>40.077 Mm — Equatorial circumference of the <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a></li>
<li>49.528 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a></li>
<li>51.118 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="100_megametres">100 megametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 100 megametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1e8m_comparison_Saturn_Jupiter_OGLE-TR-122b_with_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus_no_transparency.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1280" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/1e8m_comparison_Saturn_Jupiter_OGLE-TR-122b_with_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus_no_transparency.png/250px-1e8m_comparison_Saturn_Jupiter_OGLE-TR-122b_with_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus_no_transparency.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/1e8m_comparison_Saturn_Jupiter_OGLE-TR-122b_with_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus_no_transparency.png/375px-1e8m_comparison_Saturn_Jupiter_OGLE-TR-122b_with_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus_no_transparency.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/1e8m_comparison_Saturn_Jupiter_OGLE-TR-122b_with_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus_no_transparency.png/500px-1e8m_comparison_Saturn_Jupiter_OGLE-TR-122b_with_Uranus_Neptune_Sirius_B_Earth_Venus_no_transparency.png 2x" width="250"/></a>

The <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>-<a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a> orbit, <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OGLE-TR-122b" title="OGLE-TR-122b">OGLE-TR-122b</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_E7_m" title="1 E7 m">other objects</a>, to scale. </div>
</div>
<p>To help compare different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude" title="Orders of magnitude">orders of magnitude</a>, this page lists <a href="/wiki/Length" title="Length">lengths</a> starting at 10<sup>8</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">metres</a> (100 <a href="/wiki/Megametre" title="Megametre">megametres</a> or 100,000 <a href="/wiki/Kilometre" title="Kilometre">kilometres</a> or 62,150 <a href="/wiki/Mile" title="Mile">miles</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>102 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/HD_149026_b" title="HD 149026 b">HD 149026 b</a>, an unusually dense <a href="/wiki/Gas_giant" title="Gas giant">Jovian planet</a></li>
<li>111.191 Mm — 20,000 (nautical, British) <a href="/wiki/League_(unit)" title="League (unit)">leagues</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Jules_Verne" title="Jules Verne">Jules Verne</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Twenty_Thousand_Leagues_Under_the_Sea" title="Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea">Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea</a></i>)</li>
<li>120 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a></li>
<li>140 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a></li>
<li>174 Mm — Diameter of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OGLE-TR-122b" title="OGLE-TR-122b">OGLE-TR-122b</a>, the smallest known <a href="/wiki/Star" title="Star">star</a></li>
<li>180 Mm — Diameter of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TrES-4" title="TrES-4">TrES-4</a>, the largest known <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planet</a></li>
<li>196 Mm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Proxima_Centauri" title="Proxima Centauri">Proxima Centauri</a>, a typical <a href="/wiki/Red_dwarf" title="Red dwarf">red dwarf</a></li>
<li>299.792 Mm — One <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_second" title="Light second">light second</a>; the distance <a href="/wiki/Light" title="Light">light</a> travels in <a href="/wiki/Vacuum" title="Vacuum">vacuum</a> in one <a href="/wiki/Second" title="Second">second</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">speed of light</a>)</li>
<li>384.4 Mm (238,855 mi) — Average <a href="/wiki/Orbit_of_the_Moon" title="Orbit of the Moon">Earth-Moon distance</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-LD_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-LD-53">[51]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1_gigametre">1 gigametre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 1 gigametre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1e9m_comparison.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/1e9m_comparison.png/350px-1e9m_comparison.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/1e9m_comparison.png/525px-1e9m_comparison.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/1e9m_comparison.png/700px-1e9m_comparison.png 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1e9m_comparison.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Upper part: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamma_Orionis" title="Gamma Orionis">Gamma Orionis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algol" title="Algol">Algol B</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a> (centre), underneath their darker mirror images <span style="white-space:nowrap;">(artist's interpretation),</span> and <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_E8_m" title="1 E8 m">other objects</a>,</span> to scale.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To help compare different distances this page lists lengths starting at 10<sup>9</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">metres</a> (1 <a href="/wiki/Gigametre" title="Gigametre">gigametre</a> (Gm) or 1 billion <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">metres</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>1.4 Gm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li>1.5 Gm — <i>(proposed) Expected orbit from Earth of the <a href="/wiki/James_Webb_Space_Telescope" title="James Webb Space Telescope">James Webb Space Telescope</a></i></li>
<li>2.19 Gm — Closest approach of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comet_Lexell" title="Comet Lexell">Comet Lexell</a> to <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>, happened on 1 July 1770; closest <a href="/wiki/Comet" title="Comet">comet</a> approach on record</li>
<li>3 Gm — Total length of "wiring" in the human brain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li>4.2 Gm — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Algol" title="Algol">Algol B</a></li>
<li>5.0 Gm — Closest approach of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comet_Halley" title="Comet Halley">Comet Halley</a> to Earth, happened on 10 April 837</li>
<li><i>5.0 Gm — (proposed) Size of the arms of the giant triangle shaped Michelson interferometer of the <a href="/wiki/Laser_Interferometer_Space_Antenna" title="Laser Interferometer Space Antenna">Laser Interferometer Space Antenna</a> (LISA) planned to start observations in or around 2015.</i></li>
<li>7.9 Gm — Diameter of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamma_Orionis" title="Gamma Orionis">Gamma Orionis</a></li>
<li>9.0 Gm — Estimated diameter of the <a href="/wiki/Event_horizon" title="Event horizon">event horizon</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sagittarius_A*" title="Sagittarius A*">Sagittarius A*</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Supermassive_black_hole" title="Supermassive black hole">supermassive black hole</a> in the center of the <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way</a> galaxy</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="10_gigametres">10 gigametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 10 gigametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1e10m_comparison_Rigel,_Aldebaran,_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/1e10m_comparison_Rigel%2C_Aldebaran%2C_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png/220px-1e10m_comparison_Rigel%2C_Aldebaran%2C_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/1e10m_comparison_Rigel%2C_Aldebaran%2C_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png/330px-1e10m_comparison_Rigel%2C_Aldebaran%2C_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/1e10m_comparison_Rigel%2C_Aldebaran%2C_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png/440px-1e10m_comparison_Rigel%2C_Aldebaran%2C_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1e10m_comparison_Rigel,_Aldebaran,_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rigel and Aldebaran (top left and right) compared to smaller stars, the Sun (very small dot in lower middle, with orbit of mercury as yellow ellipse) and transparent sphere with radius of one light minute: click image for larger view and links to other scales.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To help compare different <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> this page lists lengths starting at 10<sup>10</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">metres</a> (10 <a href="/wiki/Gigametre" title="Gigametre">gigametres</a> (Gm) or 10 million <a href="/wiki/Kilometre" title="Kilometre">kilometres</a>, or 0.07 <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">Astronomical units</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>15 Gm — Closest distance of <a href="/wiki/Comet_Hyakutake" title="Comet Hyakutake">Comet Hyakutake</a> from <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a></li>
<li>18 Gm — One <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light-minute" title="Light-minute">light-minute</a> (see yellow sphere in right-hand diagram)</li>
<li>24 Gm — Radius of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heliostationary_orbit" title="Heliostationary orbit">heliostationary orbit</a></li>
<li>46 Gm — <a href="/wiki/Apsis" title="Apsis">Perihelion</a> distance of <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">Mercury</a> (yellow ellipse on the right)</li>
<li>55 Gm — 60,000-year <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perigee" title="Perigee">perigee</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> (last achieved on August 27, 2003)</li>
<li>58 Gm — Average passing distance between <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a> and Mars at the moment they overtake each other in their orbits</li>
<li>61 Gm<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aldiam_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-aldiam-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup> — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Aldebaran" title="Aldebaran">Aldebaran</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Red_giant" title="Red giant">orange giant</a> star (large star on right)</li>
<li>70 Gm — <a href="/wiki/Apsis" title="Apsis">Aphelion</a> distance of Mercury</li>
<li>76 Gm — <a href="/wiki/Neso_(moon)" title="Neso (moon)">Neso</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Apsis" title="Apsis">apocentric</a> distance; greatest distance of a <a href="/wiki/Natural_satellite" title="Natural satellite">natural satellite</a> from its parent <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planet</a> (<a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a>)</li>
<li>86 Gm<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2008)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Rigel" title="Rigel">Rigel</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_supergiant" title="Blue supergiant">blue supergiant</a> <a href="/wiki/Star" title="Star">star</a> (largest star on right)</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="100_gigametres">100 gigametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 100 gigametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1e11m_comparison_R_Doradus_and_Betelgeuse,_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/1e11m_comparison_R_Doradus_and_Betelgeuse%2C_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png/220px-1e11m_comparison_R_Doradus_and_Betelgeuse%2C_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/1e11m_comparison_R_Doradus_and_Betelgeuse%2C_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png/330px-1e11m_comparison_R_Doradus_and_Betelgeuse%2C_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/1e11m_comparison_R_Doradus_and_Betelgeuse%2C_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png/440px-1e11m_comparison_R_Doradus_and_Betelgeuse%2C_and_smaller_-_antialiased_no_transparency.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

From largest to smallest: Jupiter's orbit, red supergiant star Betelgeuse, Mars' orbit, Earth's orbit, star R Doradus, and orbits of Venus, Mercury. Inside R Doradus' depiction are the blue giant star Rigel and red giant star Aldebaran. The faint yellow glow around the Sun represents one light minute. Click image to see more details and links to their scales.</div>

<p>To help compare distances at different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude" title="Orders of magnitude">orders of magnitude</a> this page lists lengths starting at 10<sup>11</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">metres</a> (100 <a href="/wiki/Gigametre" title="Gigametre">Gm</a> or 100 million <a href="/wiki/Kilometre" title="Kilometre">kilometres</a> or 0.7 <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">astronomical units</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>109 Gm — 0.7 AU — Distance between <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a></li>
<li>149.6 Gm (93.0 million mi) — 1.0 AU — Distance between the <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a> and the Sun - the definition of the <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">astronomical unit</a></li>
<li>180 Gm — 1.2 AU — Maximum diameter of <a href="/wiki/Sagittarius_A*" title="Sagittarius A*">Sagittarius A*</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Supermassive_black_hole" title="Supermassive black hole">supermassive black hole</a> in the center of <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way</a> galaxy</li>
<li>228 Gm — 1.5 AU — Distance between <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> and the Sun</li>
<li>570 Gm — 3.8 AU — Length of the tail of <a href="/wiki/Comet_Hyakutake" title="Comet Hyakutake">Comet Hyakutake</a> measured by <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulysses_probe" title="Ulysses probe">Ulysses</a></i>; the actual value could be much higher</li>
<li>591 Gm — 4.0 AU — Minimum distance between the <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a></li>
<li>624 Gm — 4.2 AU — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Antares" title="Antares">Antares</a></li>
<li>780 Gm — 5.2 AU — Distance between Jupiter and the Sun</li>
<li>965 Gm — 6.4 AU — Maximum distance between the Earth and Jupiter</li>
</ul>

<div class="thumb tright">

8 things in the Terameter group</div>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1e12m_comparison_Kuiper_belt_and_smaller.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/1e12m_comparison_Kuiper_belt_and_smaller.png/220px-1e12m_comparison_Kuiper_belt_and_smaller.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/1e12m_comparison_Kuiper_belt_and_smaller.png/330px-1e12m_comparison_Kuiper_belt_and_smaller.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/1e12m_comparison_Kuiper_belt_and_smaller.png/440px-1e12m_comparison_Kuiper_belt_and_smaller.png 2x" width="220"/></a>

Comparison of size of the Kuiper belt (large faint torus) with the star VY Canis Majoris (at its previous estimate, within Saturn's orbit), Betelgeuse (inside Jupiter's orbit) and R Doradus (small central red sphere) together with the orbits of Neptune and Uranus, to scale. The yellow ellipses represent the orbits of each planet and the dwarf planet Pluto.</div>

<p>To help compare different <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a>, this page lists lengths starting at 10<sup>12</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> (1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terametre" title="Terametre">Tm</a> or 1 billion <a href="/wiki/Kilometre" title="Kilometre">km</a> or 6.7 <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">astronomical units</a>). Less than 1 Terameter from earth to the Sun</p>
<ul>
<li>1.079 Tm — 7.2 AU — One <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light-hour" title="Light-hour">light-hour</a></li>
<li>1.4 Tm — 9.5 AU — Distance between <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a></li>
<li>1.97 Tm — 13.2 AU — revised estimated diameter of <a href="/wiki/VY_Canis_Majoris" title="VY Canis Majoris">VY Canis Majoris</a>. The newly improved measurement was 30% lower than the previous 2007 estimate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wittkowski_vlti_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wittkowski_vlti-59">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li>2.0 Tm — 13.4 AU — Diameter of one of the largest known stars, <a href="/wiki/KY_Cygni" title="KY Cygni">KY Cygni</a></li>
<li>2.4 Tm — 15.9 AU — estimated diameter of <a href="/wiki/UY_Scuti" title="UY Scuti">UY Scuti</a>, the largest known star as of 2013</li>
<li>2.8 Tm — 18.72 AU — previous estimated diameter of <a href="/wiki/VY_Canis_Majoris" title="VY Canis Majoris">VY Canis Majoris</a>, as of 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-humphreys_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-humphreys-60">[58]</a></sup> The size was revised in 2012 through improved measurement techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wittkowski_vlti_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wittkowski_vlti-59">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li>2.9 Tm — 19.4 AU — Distance between <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a> and the Sun</li>
<li>4.4 Tm — 29.4 AU — <a href="/wiki/Apsis" title="Apsis">Perihelion</a> distance of <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a></li>
<li>4.5 Tm — 30.1 AU — Distance between <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a> and the Sun</li>
<li>4.5 Tm — 30.1 AU — Inner radius of the <a href="/wiki/Kuiper_belt" title="Kuiper belt">Kuiper belt</a></li>
<li>5.7 Tm — 38.1 AU — Perihelion distance of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/136199_Eris" title="136199 Eris">Eris</a></li>
<li>7.3 Tm — 48.8 AU — <a href="/wiki/Apsis" title="Apsis">Aphelion</a> distance of <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a></li>
<li>7.5 Tm — 50.1 AU — Outer radius of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kuiper_Belt" title="Kuiper Belt">Kuiper Belt</a>, inner boundary of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oort_Cloud" title="Oort Cloud">Oort Cloud</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="10_terametres">10 terametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 10 terametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1e13m_comparison_Hale_Bopp_and_smaller_-_HQ_no_transparency.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/1e13m_comparison_Hale_Bopp_and_smaller_-_HQ_no_transparency.png/220px-1e13m_comparison_Hale_Bopp_and_smaller_-_HQ_no_transparency.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/1e13m_comparison_Hale_Bopp_and_smaller_-_HQ_no_transparency.png/330px-1e13m_comparison_Hale_Bopp_and_smaller_-_HQ_no_transparency.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/1e13m_comparison_Hale_Bopp_and_smaller_-_HQ_no_transparency.png/440px-1e13m_comparison_Hale_Bopp_and_smaller_-_HQ_no_transparency.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1e13m_comparison_Hale_Bopp_and_smaller_-_HQ_no_transparency.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sedna's orbit (left) is longer than 100 Tm, but other lengths are between 10 and 100 Tm: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comet_Hale-Bopp" title="Comet Hale-Bopp">Comet Hale-Bopp</a>'s orbit (lower, faint orange); one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light-day" title="Light-day">light-day</a> (yellow spherical shell with yellow Vernal point arrow as radius); the heliosphere's <a href="/wiki/Heliosphere#Termination_shock" title="Heliosphere">termination shock</a> (blue shell); and other arrows show positions of <a href="/wiki/Voyager_1" title="Voyager 1">Voyager 1</a> (red) and <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_10" title="Pioneer 10">Pioneer 10</a> (green). Click on image for larger view and links to other scales.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To help compare different <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> this page lists lengths starting at 10<sup>13</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> (10 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terametre" title="Terametre">Tm</a> or 10 billion <a href="/wiki/Kilometre" title="Kilometre">km</a> or 67 <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">astronomical units</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>11.1 Tm — 74.2 AU — Distance that <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_1" title="Voyager 1">Voyager 1</a></i> began detecting returning particles from <a href="/wiki/Heliosphere#Termination_shock" title="Heliosphere">termination shock</a></li>
<li>11.4 Tm — 76.2 AU — <a href="/wiki/Apsis" title="Apsis">Perihelion</a> distance of <a href="/wiki/90377_Sedna" title="90377 Sedna">90377 Sedna</a></li>
<li>12.1 Tm — 70 to 90 AU — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Heliosphere#Termination_shock" title="Heliosphere">termination shock</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_1" title="Voyager 1">Voyager 1</a></i> crossed at 94 AU)</li>
<li>12.9 Tm — 86.3 AU — Distance to 90377 Sedna in March 2014</li>
<li>13.2 Tm — 88.6 AU — Distance to <i><a href="/wiki/Pioneer_11" title="Pioneer 11">Pioneer 11</a></i> in March 2014</li>
<li>14.1 Tm — 94.3 AU — Estimated radius of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_system" title="Solar system">solar system</a></li>
<li>14.4 Tm — 96.4 AU — Distance to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/136199_Eris" title="136199 Eris">Eris</a> in March 2014 (now near its <a href="/wiki/Apsis" title="Apsis">aphelion</a>)</li>
<li>15.1 Tm — 101 AU — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Heliosphere#Heliosheath" title="Heliosphere">heliosheath</a></li>
<li>16.5 Tm — 111 AU — Distance to <i><a href="/wiki/Pioneer_10" title="Pioneer 10">Pioneer 10</a></i> in March 2014</li>
<li>16.6 Tm - 111.2AU - Distance to <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a></i> in May 2016</li>
<li>20.0 Tm - 135 AU - Distance to <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_1" title="Voyager 1">Voyager 1</a></i> in May 2016</li>
<li>25.9 Tm — 172 AU — One <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light-day" title="Light-day">light-day</a></li>
<li>55.7 Tm — 371 AU — Aphelion distance of the <a href="/wiki/Comet" title="Comet">comet</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hale-Bopp" title="Hale-Bopp">Hale-Bopp</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="100_terametres">100 terametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 100 terametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1e14m_comparison_light_day_week_and_month.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/1e14m_comparison_light_day_week_and_month.png/220px-1e14m_comparison_light_day_week_and_month.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/1e14m_comparison_light_day_week_and_month.png/330px-1e14m_comparison_light_day_week_and_month.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/1e14m_comparison_light_day_week_and_month.png/440px-1e14m_comparison_light_day_week_and_month.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1e14m_comparison_light_day_week_and_month.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The largest yellow sphere indicates one light month distance from the Sun. Click the image for larger view, more details and links to other scales.</div>
</div>

<div class="hatnote plainlinks" role="note">This list is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">incomplete</a>; you can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit">expanding it</a>.</div>
<p>To help compare different <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> this page lists lengths starting at 10<sup>14</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> (100 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terametre" title="Terametre">Tm</a> or 100,000 million <a href="/wiki/Kilometre" title="Kilometre">km</a> or 670 <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">astronomical units</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>146 Tm — 975 AU — <a href="/wiki/Apsis" title="Apsis">Aphelion</a> distance of <a href="/wiki/90377_Sedna" title="90377 Sedna">90377 Sedna</a></li>
<li>172 TM — 1150 AU — <a href="/wiki/Schwarzschild_radius" title="Schwarzschild radius">Schwarzschild diameter</a> of <a href="/wiki/H1821%2B643" title="H1821+643">H1821+643</a>, one of the most massive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_holes" title="Black holes">black holes</a> known</li>
<li>181 Tm — 1210 AU — One <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light-week" title="Light-week">light-week</a></li>
<li>653 Tm — 4367 AU — Aphelion distance of <a href="/wiki/Comet" title="Comet">comet</a> <a href="/wiki/Comet_Hyakutake" title="Comet Hyakutake">Hyakutake</a> (current <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">orbit</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup></li>
<li>757 Tm — 5059 AU — radius of the <a href="/wiki/Stingray_Nebula" title="Stingray Nebula">Stingray Nebula</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parthasarathy2000_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Parthasarathy2000-62">[60]</a></sup></li>
<li>777 Tm — 5180 AU — One <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light-month" title="Light-month">light-month</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1_petametre">1 petametre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: 1 petametre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1e15m_comparison_cat%27s_eye_nebula_barnard_68_one_light_year.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1280" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/1e15m_comparison_cat%27s_eye_nebula_barnard_68_one_light_year.png/220px-1e15m_comparison_cat%27s_eye_nebula_barnard_68_one_light_year.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/1e15m_comparison_cat%27s_eye_nebula_barnard_68_one_light_year.png/330px-1e15m_comparison_cat%27s_eye_nebula_barnard_68_one_light_year.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/1e15m_comparison_cat%27s_eye_nebula_barnard_68_one_light_year.png/440px-1e15m_comparison_cat%27s_eye_nebula_barnard_68_one_light_year.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1e15m_comparison_cat%27s_eye_nebula_barnard_68_one_light_year.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Largest circle with yellow arrow indicates one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light year</a> from <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a>; <a href="/wiki/Cat%27s_Eye_Nebula" title="Cat's Eye Nebula">Cat's Eye Nebula</a> on left and <a href="/wiki/Barnard_68" title="Barnard 68">Barnard 68</a> in middle are depicted in front of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comet_1910_A1" title="Comet 1910 A1">Comet 1910 A1</a>'s orbit. Click image for larger view, details and links to other scales.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To help compare different <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> this page lists lengths starting at 10<sup>15</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> (1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petametre" title="Petametre">Pm</a> or 1,000,000 million <a href="/wiki/Kilometre" title="Kilometre">km</a> or 6685 <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">astronomical units</a> (AU) or 0.11 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light years</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>1.0 Pm = 0.105702341 light years <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup></li>
<li>1.9 Pm ± .5 Pm = 12,000 AU = 0.2 light year radius of <a href="/wiki/Cat%27s_Eye_Nebula" title="Cat's Eye Nebula">Cat's Eye Nebula</a>'s inner core<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cat_calc_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cat_calc-64">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>4.7 Pm = 30,000 AU = half light year diameter of <a href="/wiki/Bok_globule" title="Bok globule">Bok globule</a> <a href="/wiki/Barnard_68" title="Barnard 68">Barnard 68</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Szpir_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Szpir-65">[63]</a></sup></li>
<li>7.5 Pm — 50,000 AU — Possible outer boundary of <a href="/wiki/Oort_cloud" title="Oort cloud">Oort cloud</a> (other estimates are 75,000 to 125,000 or even 189,000 <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">AU</a> (1.6, 2, and 3 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light years</a>, respectively))</li>
<li>7.7 Pm — 52,000 AU — <a href="/wiki/Apsis" title="Apsis">Aphelion</a> distance of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Daylight_Comet_of_1910" title="Great Daylight Comet of 1910">Great Daylight Comet of 1910</a></li>
<li>9.5 Pm — 63,241.1 AU — One <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light year</a>, the distance travelled by light in one year</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="10_petametres">10 petametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: 10 petametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
