<p>To help compare different distances this page lists lengths starting at 10<sup>16</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> (10 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petametre" title="Petametre">Pm</a> or 66,800 <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">AU</a>, 1.06 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light years</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>15 Pm — 1.59 light years — Possible outer radius of <a href="/wiki/Oort_cloud" title="Oort cloud">Oort cloud</a></li>
<li>20 Pm — 2.11 light years — maximum extent of influence of the Sun's <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_field" title="Gravitational field">gravitational field</a></li>
<li>30.9 Pm — 3.26 light years — 1 <a href="/wiki/Parsec" title="Parsec">parsec</a></li>
<li>39.9 Pm — 4.22 light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Proxima_Centauri" title="Proxima Centauri">Proxima Centauri</a> (nearest star to <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a>)</li>
<li>81.3 Pm — 8.59 light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Sirius" title="Sirius">Sirius</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="100_petametres">100 petametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: 100 petametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1e17m_comparison_100_light_years_nebula_clusters.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1280" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/1e17m_comparison_100_light_years_nebula_clusters.png/220px-1e17m_comparison_100_light_years_nebula_clusters.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/1e17m_comparison_100_light_years_nebula_clusters.png/330px-1e17m_comparison_100_light_years_nebula_clusters.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/1e17m_comparison_100_light_years_nebula_clusters.png/440px-1e17m_comparison_100_light_years_nebula_clusters.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1e17m_comparison_100_light_years_nebula_clusters.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lengths with order of magnitude 1e17m: yellow Vernal Point arrow traces hundred light year radius circle with smaller ten light year circle at right; globular cluster Messier 5 in background; 12 light year radius Orion Nebula middle right; 50 light year wide view of the Carina Nebula bottom left; Pleiades cluster and Bubble nebula with similar diameters each around 10 light years bottom right; grey arrows show distances from Sun to stars Aldebaran (65 light years) and Vega (25 light years).</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote plainlinks" role="note">This list is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">incomplete</a>; you can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit">expanding it</a>.</div>
<p>To help compare different <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> this page lists lengths between 10<sup>17</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> (100 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petametre" title="Petametre">Pm</a> or 11 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light years</a>) and 10<sup>18</sup> m (106 light years).</p>
<ul>
<li>110 Pm — 12 light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Tau_Ceti" title="Tau Ceti">Tau Ceti</a></li>
<li>230 Pm — 24 light years — Diameter of the <a href="/wiki/Orion_Nebula" title="Orion Nebula">Orion Nebula</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apj667_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-apj667-66">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li>240 Pm — 25 light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Vega" title="Vega">Vega</a></li>
<li>260 Pm — 27 light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Beta_Canum_Venaticorum" title="Beta Canum Venaticorum">Chara</a>, a star approximately as bright as our Sun. Its faintness gives us an idea how our <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a> would appear when viewed from even so close a distance as this.</li>
<li>350 Pm — 37 light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Arcturus" title="Arcturus">Arcturus</a></li>
<li>400 Pm — 42 light years — Distance to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capella_(star)" title="Capella (star)">Capella</a></li>
<li>620 Pm — 65 light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Aldebaran" title="Aldebaran">Aldebaran</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1_exametre">1 exametre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: 1 exametre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1e18m_comparison_1000_light_years_nebula_clusters.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1280" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/1e18m_comparison_1000_light_years_nebula_clusters.png/220px-1e18m_comparison_1000_light_years_nebula_clusters.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/1e18m_comparison_1000_light_years_nebula_clusters.png/330px-1e18m_comparison_1000_light_years_nebula_clusters.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/1e18m_comparison_1000_light_years_nebula_clusters.png/440px-1e18m_comparison_1000_light_years_nebula_clusters.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1e18m_comparison_1000_light_years_nebula_clusters.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lengths with order of magnitude 1e18m: thousand light year radius circle with yellow arrow and 100 light year circle at right with globular cluster Messier 5 within and Carina Nebula in front; globular cluster Omega Centauri to left of both; part of the 1400 light year wide Tarantula Nebula fills the background.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This list includes distances between 1 and 10 <b>exametres</b> (10<sup>18</sup> m). To help compare different <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> this page lists lengths between 10<sup>18</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> (1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exametre" title="Exametre">Em</a> or 105.7 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light years</a>) and 10<sup>19</sup> m (1057 light years).</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">1.4 Em — 145 light years — Diameter of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Messier_Object_13" title="Messier Object 13">Messier Object 13</a> (a typical <a href="/wiki/Globular_cluster" title="Globular cluster">globular cluster</a>)</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>1.6 Em — 172 ± 12.5 light years — Diameter of <a href="/wiki/Omega_Centauri" title="Omega Centauri">Omega Centauri</a> (one of the largest known <a href="/wiki/Globular_cluster" title="Globular cluster">globular clusters</a>, perhaps containing over a million <a href="/wiki/Star" title="Star">stars</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vandeVenetal2006_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-vandeVenetal2006-69">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">3.1 Em — 310 light years — Distance to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canopus_(star)" title="Canopus (star)">Canopus</a> according to <i><a href="/wiki/Hipparcos" title="Hipparcos">Hipparcos</a></i></span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>6.1 Em — 640 light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Betelgeuse" title="Betelgeuse">Betelgeuse</a> according to <i>Hipparcos</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HARPER_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-HARPER-70">[68]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">6.2 Em — 650 light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Helix_Nebula" title="Helix Nebula">Helix Nebula</a>, located in the constellation <a href="/wiki/Aquarius_(constellation)" title="Aquarius (constellation)">Aquarius</a></span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">7.3 Em — 730 light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Rigel" title="Rigel">Rigel</a> according to <i>Hipparcos</i></span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">9 Em — 1000 light years — Diameter of the <a href="/wiki/Tarantula_Nebula" title="Tarantula Nebula">Tarantula Nebula</a></span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="10_exametres">10 exametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: 10 exametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>To help compare different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude" title="Orders of magnitude">orders of magnitude</a>, this page lists <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> starting at 10 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exametre" title="Exametre">Em</a> (10<sup>19</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> or 1,100 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light years</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>13 Em — 1,300 light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Orion_Nebula" title="Orion Nebula">Orion Nebula</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup></li>
<li>14 Em — 1,500 light years — Approximate thickness of the <a href="/wiki/Galactic_plane" title="Galactic plane">plane</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way</a> <a href="/wiki/Galaxy" title="Galaxy">galaxy</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a>'s location</li>
<li>30.8568 Em — 3,261.6 light years — 1 <a href="/wiki/Parsec" title="Parsec">kiloparsec</a></li>
<li>31 Em — 3,200 light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Deneb" title="Deneb">Deneb</a> according to <i><a href="/wiki/Hipparcos" title="Hipparcos">Hipparcos</a></i></li>
<li>46 Em — 4,900 light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/OGLE-TR-56" title="OGLE-TR-56">OGLE-TR-56</a>, the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planet" title="Extrasolar planet">extrasolar planet</a> discovered using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planet#Transit_method" title="Extrasolar planet">transit method</a></li>
<li>47 Em — 5,000 light years — Distance to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boomerang_nebula" title="Boomerang nebula">Boomerang nebula</a>, coldest place known (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_E0_K" title="1 E0 K">1 K</a>)</li>
<li>53 Em — 5,600 light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Globular_cluster" title="Globular cluster">globular cluster</a> <a href="/wiki/Messier_4" title="Messier 4">M4</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planet" title="Extrasolar planet">extrasolar planet</a> <a href="/wiki/PSR_B1620-26_b" title="PSR B1620-26 b">PSR B1620-26 b</a> within it</li>
<li>61 Em — 6,500 light years — Distance to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perseus_Spiral_Arm" title="Perseus Spiral Arm">Perseus Spiral Arm</a> (next spiral arm out in the Milky Way galaxy)</li>
<li>71 Em — 7,500 light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Eta_Carinae" title="Eta Carinae">Eta Carinae</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="100_exametres">100 exametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: 100 exametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>To help compare different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude" title="Orders of magnitude">orders of magnitude</a>, this page lists <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> starting at 100 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exametre" title="Exametre">Em</a> (10<sup>20</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> or 11,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light years</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>150 Em — 16,000 light years — Diameter of the <a href="/wiki/Small_Magellanic_Cloud" title="Small Magellanic Cloud">Small Magellanic Cloud</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_galaxy" title="Dwarf galaxy">dwarf galaxy</a> orbiting the <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way</a></li>
<li>200 Em — 21,500 light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb" title="OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb">OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb</a>, the most distant and the most <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>-like <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planet</a> known</li>
<li>240 Em — 25,000 light years — Distance to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canis_Major_Dwarf_Galaxy" title="Canis Major Dwarf Galaxy">Canis Major Dwarf Galaxy</a></li>
<li>260 Em — 28,000 light years — Distance to the center of the <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Galaxy</a></li>
<li>830 Em — 88,000 light years — Distance to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sagittarius_Dwarf_Elliptical_Galaxy" title="Sagittarius Dwarf Elliptical Galaxy">Sagittarius Dwarf Elliptical Galaxy</a></li>
<li>950 Em — 100,000 light years — Diameter of the disc of the <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way Galaxy</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1_zettametre">1 zettametre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: 1 zettametre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <b>zettametre</b> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SI" title="SI">SI</a> symbol: <b>Zm</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Units_of_measurement" title="Units of measurement">unit</a> of <a href="/wiki/Length" title="Length">length</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Metric_system" title="Metric system">metric system</a> equal to 10<sup>21</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">metres</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bipm.org_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-bipm.org-72">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>To help compare different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude" title="Orders of magnitude">orders of magnitude</a>, this page lists <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> starting at 1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zettametre" title="Zettametre">Zm</a> (10<sup>21</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> or 110,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light years</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>1.7 Zm — 179,000 light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Large_Magellanic_Cloud" title="Large Magellanic Cloud">Large Magellanic Cloud</a>, largest <a href="/wiki/Satellite_galaxy" title="Satellite galaxy">satellite galaxy</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way</a></li>
<li>2.0 Zm — 210,000 light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Small_Magellanic_Cloud" title="Small Magellanic Cloud">Small Magellanic Cloud</a></li>
<li>2.8 Zm — 300,000 light years — Distance to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intergalactic_Wanderer" title="Intergalactic Wanderer">Intergalactic Wanderer</a>, one of the most distant <a href="/wiki/Globular_cluster" title="Globular cluster">globular clusters</a> of Milky Way</li>
<li>8.5 Zm — 900,000 light years — Distance to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leo_I_Dwarf_Galaxy" title="Leo I Dwarf Galaxy">Leo I Dwarf Galaxy</a>, farthest known <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way</a> satellite <a href="/wiki/Galaxy" title="Galaxy">galaxy</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="10_zettametres">10 zettametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: 10 zettametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>To help compare different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude" title="Orders of magnitude">orders of magnitude</a>, this page lists <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> starting at 10 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zettametre" title="Zettametre">Zm</a> (10<sup>22</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> or 1.1 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light years</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>24 Zm — 2.5 million light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Andromeda_Galaxy" title="Andromeda Galaxy">Andromeda Galaxy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li>30.8568 Zm — 3.2616 million light years — 1 <a href="/wiki/Parsec" title="Parsec">megaparsec</a></li>
<li>40 Zm — 4.2 million light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/IC_10" title="IC 10">IC 10</a>, a distant member of the <a href="/wiki/Local_Group" title="Local Group">Local Group</a> of <a href="/wiki/Galaxy" title="Galaxy">galaxies</a></li>
<li>49.2 Zm — 5.2 million light years — Width of the <a href="/wiki/Local_Group" title="Local Group">Local Group</a> of <a href="/wiki/Galaxy" title="Galaxy">galaxies</a></li>
<li>57 Zm — 6 million light years — Diameter of the supergiant <a href="/wiki/Elliptical_galaxy" title="Elliptical galaxy">elliptical galaxy</a> <a href="/wiki/IC_1101" title="IC 1101">IC 1101</a></li>
<li>95 Zm — 10 million light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Sculptor_Galaxy" title="Sculptor Galaxy">Sculptor Galaxy</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sculptor_Group" title="Sculptor Group">Sculptor Group</a> of galaxies</li>
<li>95 Zm — 10 million light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Maffei_1" title="Maffei 1">Maffei 1</a>, the nearest giant <a href="/wiki/Elliptical_galaxy" title="Elliptical galaxy">elliptical galaxy</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maffei_1_group_of_galaxies" title="Maffei 1 group of galaxies">Maffei 1 Group</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="100_zettametres">100 zettametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: 100 zettametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>To help compare different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude" title="Orders of magnitude">orders of magnitude</a>, this page lists <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> starting at 100 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zettametre" title="Zettametre">Zm</a> (10<sup>23</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> or 11 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light years</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>140 Zm — 15 million light years — Distance to <a href="/wiki/Centaurus_A" title="Centaurus A">Centaurus A</a> galaxy</li>
<li>250 Zm — 27 million light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Pinwheel_Galaxy" title="Pinwheel Galaxy">Pinwheel Galaxy</a></li>
<li>280 Zm — 30 million light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Sombrero_Galaxy" title="Sombrero Galaxy">Sombrero Galaxy</a></li>
<li>570 Zm — 60 million light years — Approximate distance to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virgo_cluster" title="Virgo cluster">Virgo cluster</a>, nearest <a href="/wiki/Galaxy_cluster" title="Galaxy cluster">galaxy cluster</a></li>
<li>620 Zm — 65 million light years — Approximate distance to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fornax_cluster" title="Fornax cluster">Fornax cluster</a></li>
<li>800 Zm — 85 million light years — Approximate distance to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eridanus_cluster" title="Eridanus cluster">Eridanus cluster</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1_yottametre">1 yottametre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: 1 yottametre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <b>yottametre</b> or <b>yottameter</b> in the US ( <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SI" title="SI">SI</a> symbol: <b>Ym</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Units_of_measurement" title="Units of measurement">unit</a> of <a href="/wiki/Length" title="Length">length</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Metric_system" title="Metric system">metric system</a> equal to 10<sup>24</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">metres</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bipm.org_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-bipm.org-72">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>To help compare different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude" title="Orders of magnitude">orders of magnitude</a>, this page lists <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> starting at 1 Ym (10<sup>24</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> or 105.702 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light years</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>1.2 Ym — 127 million light years — Distance to the closest observed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamma_ray_burst" title="Gamma ray burst">gamma ray burst</a> <a href="/wiki/GRB_980425" title="GRB 980425">GRB 980425</a></li>
<li>1.3 Ym — 137 million light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Centaurus_Cluster" title="Centaurus Cluster">Centaurus Cluster</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galaxies" title="Galaxies">galaxies</a>, the nearest large <a href="/wiki/Supercluster" title="Supercluster">supercluster</a></li>
<li>1.9 Ym — 201 million light years — Diameter of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Local_Supercluster" title="Local Supercluster">Local Supercluster</a></li>
<li>2.3 Ym — 225 to 250 million light years — Distance light travels in vacuum in one <a href="/wiki/Galactic_year" title="Galactic year">galactic year</a></li>
<li>2.8 Ym — 296 million light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Coma_Cluster" title="Coma Cluster">Coma Cluster</a></li>
<li>3.2 Ym — 338 million light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Stephan%27s_Quintet" title="Stephan's Quintet">Stephan's Quintet</a></li>
<li>4.7 Ym — 496 million light years — Length of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Wall_(astronomy)" title="Great Wall (astronomy)">CfA2 Great Wall</a>, one of the largest observed superstructures in the <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">Universe</a></li>
<li>6.1 Ym — 645 million light years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Shapley_Supercluster" title="Shapley Supercluster">Shapley Supercluster</a></li>
<li>9.5 Ym — 996 million light years — Diameter of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eridanus_Supervoid" title="Eridanus Supervoid">Eridanus Supervoid</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="10_yottametres">10 yottametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: 10 yottametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Superclusters_atlasoftheuniverse.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="640" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Superclusters_atlasoftheuniverse.gif/220px-Superclusters_atlasoftheuniverse.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Superclusters_atlasoftheuniverse.gif/330px-Superclusters_atlasoftheuniverse.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Superclusters_atlasoftheuniverse.gif/440px-Superclusters_atlasoftheuniverse.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Superclusters_atlasoftheuniverse.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The universe within 1 billion light years of Earth</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To help compare different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude" title="Orders of magnitude">orders of magnitude</a>, this page lists <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> starting at 10 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yottametre" title="Yottametre">Ym</a> (10<sup>25</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> or 1.1 billion <a href="/wiki/Light-year" title="Light-year">light-years</a>). At this scale, expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">universe</a> becomes significant. Distance of these objects are derived from their measured <a href="/wiki/Redshift" title="Redshift">redshifts</a>, which depends on the <a href="/wiki/Physical_cosmology" title="Physical cosmology">cosmological</a> models used.</p>
<ul>
<li>13.7 Ym — 1.37 billion light-years — Length of the <a href="/wiki/Sloan_Great_Wall" title="Sloan Great Wall">Sloan Great Wall</a></li>
<li>18 Ym — redshift 0.16 — 1.9 billion light-years — Distance to the <a href="/wiki/Quasar" title="Quasar">quasar</a> <a href="/wiki/3C_273" title="3C 273">3C 273</a> (<a href="/wiki/Distance_measures_(cosmology)#Types_of_distance_measures" title="Distance measures (cosmology)">light travel distance</a>)</li>
<li>33 Ym — 3.5 billion light-years — Maximum distance of the <a href="/wiki/2dF_Galaxy_Redshift_Survey" title="2dF Galaxy Redshift Survey">2dF Galaxy Redshift Survey</a> (light travel distance)</li>
<li>37.8 Ym — 4 billion light-years — Length of the <a href="/wiki/Huge-LQG" title="Huge-LQG">Huge-LQG</a>, one of the largest and most massive known cosmic structure.</li>
<li>75 Ym — redshift 0.95 — 8 billion light-years — Approximate distance to the <a href="/wiki/Supernova" title="Supernova">supernova</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=SN_2002dd&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="SN 2002dd (page does not exist)">SN 2002dd</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hubble_Deep_Field_North" title="Hubble Deep Field North">Hubble Deep Field North</a> (light travel distance)</li>
<li>85 Ym — redshift 1.6 — 9 billion light-years — Approximate distance to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamma_ray_burst" title="Gamma ray burst">gamma ray burst</a> <a href="/wiki/GRB_990123" title="GRB 990123">GRB 990123</a> (light travel distance)</li>
<li>94.6 Ym — 10 billion light-years — Approximate distance to quasar <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=OQ172&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="OQ172 (page does not exist)">OQ172</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="100_yottametres">100 yottametres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: 100 yottametres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>To help compare different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude" title="Orders of magnitude">orders of magnitude</a>, this page lists <a href="/wiki/Distance" title="Distance">distances</a> greater than 100 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yottametre" title="Yottametre">Ym</a> (10<sup>26</sup> <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> or 11 billion <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_year" title="Light year">light years</a>). At this scale, expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">universe</a> becomes significant. Distance of these objects are derived from their measured <a href="/wiki/Redshift" title="Redshift">redshifts</a>, which depends on the <a href="/wiki/Physical_cosmology" title="Physical cosmology">cosmological</a> models used.</p>
<p>Distances longer than 100 Ym</p>
<ul>
<li>130 Ym — redshift 6.41 — 13 billion light years — <a href="/wiki/Distance_measures_(cosmology)#Types_of_distance_measures" title="Distance measures (cosmology)">Light travel distance</a> (LTD) to the <a href="/wiki/Quasar" title="Quasar">quasar</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_quasars" title="List of quasars">SDSS J1148+5251</a></li>
<li>130 Ym — redshift 1000 — 13.7 billion light years — Distance (LTD) to the source of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmic_microwave_background_radiation" title="Cosmic microwave background radiation">cosmic microwave background radiation</a>; radius of the observable <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">universe</a> measured as a LTD</li>
<li>260 Ym — 27.4 billion light years — Diameter of the observable universe (double LTD)</li>
<li>440 Ym — 46 billion light years — Radius of the universe measured as a <a href="/wiki/Comoving_distance" title="Comoving distance">comoving distance</a>.</li>
<li>590 Ym — 62 billion light years — Cosmological <a href="/wiki/Event_horizon" title="Event horizon">event horizon</a>: the largest comoving distance from which light will ever reach us (the observer) at any time in the future</li>
<li>&lt;1,000 Ym (1 kYm <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-SI_unit_prefixes#Metric_prefixes_that_were_obsoleted_or_withdrawn_from_the_SI_standard" title="Non-SI unit prefixes">in older usage</a>, or 1 brontometer in unofficial nomenclature) — Size of universe beyond the <a href="/wiki/Observable_universe" title="Observable universe">cosmic light horizon</a>, depending on its curvature; if the curvature is zero (i.e. the universe is spatially flat), the value can be <a href="/wiki/Infinity#Infinity_in_cosmology" title="Infinity">infinite</a> (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shape_of_the_Universe" title="Shape of the Universe">shape of the Universe</a>)</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orders_of_magnitude_(length)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-Asteroid-planet.3F-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Asteroid-planet.3F_32-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The exact <a href="/wiki/Solar_System#Terminology" title="Solar System">category</a> (asteroid, dwarf planet or planet) to which particular Solar System objects belong, has been subject to some revision since the discovery of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planet" title="Extrasolar planet">extrasolar planets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trans-Neptunian_object" title="Trans-Neptunian object">trans-Neptunian</a> objects</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-exponents-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-exponents_43-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-exponents_43-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">10<sup>115</sup> is 1 followed by 115 zeroes, or a <a href="/wiki/Googol" title="Googol">googol</a> multiplied by a quadrillion. 10<sup>10<sup>115</sup></sup> is 1 followed by a quadrillion googol zeroes. 10<sup>10<sup>10<sup>122</sup></sup></sup>is 1 followed by 10<sup>10<sup>122</sup></sup> (a <a href="/wiki/Googolplex" title="Googolplex">googolplex</a><sup>10 sextillion</sup>) zeroes.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>

<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">gravitational waves that originate tens of millions of light years from Earth are expected to distort the 4 kilometer mirror spacing by about 10<sup>−18</sup> m, less than one-thousandth the <a href="/wiki/Charge_radius" title="Charge radius">charge diameter</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">proton</a>. Equivalently, this is a relative change in distance of approximately one part in 10<sup>21</sup>. "On September 14, 2015 at 09:50:45 UTC the two detectors of the Laser Interferometer Gravitational-Wave Observatory simultaneously observed a transient gravitational-wave signal. The signal sweeps upwards in frequency from 35 to 250 Hz with a peak gravitational-wave strain of 1.0×10<sup>−21</sup>." B. P. Abbott et al. (LIGO Scientific Collaboration and Virgo Collaboration), "Observation of Gravitational Waves from a Binary Black Hole Merger", <i>Phys. Rev. Lett. 116, 061102</i>, published 11 February 2016.</span></li>
